Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
The Hanafi Position on Verb Takhsis: Analysis of 'لا آكل'
A detailed Hanafi-Shafi'i usul dispute on verb specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that a verb without a qarina denotes the essence (mutlaq) and cannot be specified to a particular object, and identify the Shafi'i counterargument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A verb's implicit masdar indicates the nature of the act, not individuals; without a qarina, the verb remains mutlaq.

This passage presents a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerning the interpretation of verbs like 'لا آكل'. The Hanafis argue that the verb is mutlaq and cannot be restricted to a specific object without a contextual indicator, while the Shafi'is draw an analogy to explicit masdars with tanwin. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to linguistic indications and the role of qarina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic issue
Focus on the phrase 'لا آكل' and whether it negates all eating or a specific eating. What does the verb alone indicate?
The verb is transitive, but that alone does not specify an object.
2
State the Shafi'i position and their analogy
The Shafi'is claim that 'لا آكل' is like 'لا آكل أكلاً' where the explicit masdar with tanwin can be specified to a particular eating. They argue that the verb similarly allows takhsis.
Their qiyas is based on the similarity of structure.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the analogy
The Hanafis deny the similarity: the implicit masdar in the verb indicates only the essence of the act, not any individual instance. The explicit masdar with tanwin indicates an individual (fard). Therefore, the analogy fails.
Grammarians confirm that the emphatic masdar is not for type or number.
4
Recognize the role of qarina
Without a contextual indicator (qarina), the verb remains mutlaq. A qarina is required to restrict the verb to a specific object or type. Transitivity alone does not serve as a qarina.
The discussion assumes no qarina is present.
5
Apply the principle to practical cases
In oaths or vows, saying 'لا آكل' applies to all eatables. The speaker's unexpressed intention to specify a particular food is ineffective without a qarina. This contrasts with the Shafi'i view that allows specification by intention.
Practical consequence (thamarah) of the ikhtilaf.

لما لازماً له في الاستعمال فلا يصح تفسيره بمخصص لأنه مقيد ليس مدلولا له بإحدى الدلالات ولا قرينة عليه، فلا يجوز أيضاً قد يقال الشافعية يقولون إن التقدير ضروري لأن المفعول من لوازم الفعل فلا يقنعون على أن الأكل مطلق بل يمنعونه، ولو قيل: إن خصوص لا آكل يفيد نفي الأكل المطلق عرفاً يقال : لو سلم فلا كلام في خصوص هذا الفعل ودفعه ظاهر، فإن التقييد بالمفعول به ليس في اللفظ فلا بد من قرينة زائدة دالة عليه وعلى خصوصه، وليست إذ الكلام فيما لا قرينة على تقدير المفعول به، وأما كون الفعل متعدياً فلا يصلح قرينة مر أنه كثيراً ما ينزل منزلة اللازم، وإذا لم يثبت قرينة دالة على التقييد بالمفعول بقي الفعل مطلقاً، والمطلق لا دلالة له على الخاص بوجه من الوجوه فافهم (ومنع) الشيخ ابن الحاجب الإطلاق أي إطلاق الفعل الاستحالة وجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج فالمطلق لا يكون موجوداً (مدفوع بما تقرر في مقره أن المشتقات تدل على الطبيعة من حيث هي هي)، ولا دخل فيه لوجود الكلي الطبيعي ،وعدمه، فالإطلاق ثابت ولا مجال للمنع (وبما حقق من وجود (الكلي) الطبيعي بعين وجود (الأفراد والمراد به الطبيعة من حيث هي لا هي من حيث الإطلاق حتى ينافي الوجود كما زعم هذا الشافعية قالوا لا آكل مثل لا آكل أكلاً والثاني يقبل) التخصيص (بالاتفاق) فكذا الأول (قلنا إن المماثلة ممنوعة و أن أكلاً يدل على فرد ما فإنه مصدر منون) وهو للفرد المنتشر (فلو فسر بمعين قبل وأما الفعل فهو للحقيقة من حيث هي هي من غير دلالة على الفردية فتفسيره ببعض (الأفراد دون بعض (لا يقبل فتدبر) فإن قيل : المنون أيضاً مطلق فلا يجوز تفسيره بمعين كالمصدر المفهوم في الفعل، وأيضاً إن المصدر مؤكد، فالمعنى المفهوم في الفعل ومدلول المصدر المصرح ،واحد قلت : المصدر المفهوم في الفعل من حيث هو لا يجوز تقييده لعدم الدلالة على الفردية المنوّن فدال على الفردية وقد يراد مطلق الفردية وهو حقيقة فيها، وقد يراد فرد خاص وهو مجاز فيه وكونه للتأكيد ليس حتماً فيه بل قد يكون لبيان النوع أو العدد فيجوز أن يراد نوع خاص أو عدد خاص، وأما المصدر المفهوم في الفعل فليس صالحاً لأن يراد به فرد ما أصلاً، فإن الفردية أهلاً وأما المصدر تنافي الاشتقاق منه، فإن قلت : أليس علماء البيان قالوا : إن في الفعل استعارة تبعية، وما تلك إلا لتصرف في المصدر المفهوم في الفعل، وقد أبيتم ههنا من إرادة المقيد عن المصدر المذكور؟ فالجواب عنه أنا لا نمنع التجوز في المصدر المشتق منه ليتجوز بحسبه في الفعل، وإنما نمنع تقييد المصدر المفهوم في الفعل إذ المقيد لا يصلح لكونه مشتقاً منه، منه، ولا ولا يصلح للانتساب إلى ذوات كثيرة على ما هو حاصل المشتق والاستعارة التبعية هي الأول، والممنوع هو الثاني فتأمل، ثم إنهم قالوا يلزم على هذا أن لا يصح نية السفر في لا يخرج ولا نية الثلاث في بائن أجاب بقوله (أقول : اعلم أن بعض الطبائع يكون مشككاً فيكون في بعض أشد وفي بعض أضعف فهو في حد حقيقته متنوع يقبل التجزي وتتفاوت الأحكام، فلو نوى مرتبة من مراتبه صح) تجوزاً كالخروج سفراً وغيره فإنه مشكك فيهما فإرادة السفر من الخروج صحيحة (والبينونة خفيفة وغليظة فيصح إرادة أحد النوعين (فافهم) وفيه شيء فإن المتواطىء كالمشكك المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية في إرادة بعض هذا الحكم، لأن نسبة الأفراد إلى المتواطىء كنسبتها إلى المشكك، فكما يصح المراتب من المشكك تجوزاً، كذلك يجوز في المتواطىء، فلا فرق بين لا آكل وبين يخرج، فالحق إذن أن يقال : إن الفرد الحاصل من التقييد بالمفعول لا يجوز إرادتها في آكل، فلا يجوز إرادة آكل تفاحة أو خبزاً، فإن التقييد بالمفعول غير ملحوظ للمتكلم لكونه محذوفاً نسياً منسياً، وكذا لا يجوز إرادة هذه الأفراد من الخروج في لا يخرج فلا يراد الخروج إلى كوفة أو بصرة، وإنما يجوز فيه إرادة بعض الأنواع فإنه تصرف في المنطوق فإنها أفراد لا بالنسبة إلى المفعول، ولا يجوز أن يراد أفراد الأكل مع قطع النظر عن التقييد بمأكول أيضاً، لأن حقيقته ليست إلا حركة خاصة للحيين ولا يراد خصوصيات هذه الحركة عرفاً، وليس الكلام ههنا في إرادة هذه الإفراد بخلاف ما إذا صرح بالمصدر فإنه مصدر منون وهو قد يكون لبيان النوع، فيجوز أن يعتبر التنوع باعتبار التقييد بالمفعول المأكول وإما لا آكل فليس فيه المصدر للتنويع ، ألا ترى أن النحاة أجمعوا على أن المصدر المؤكد لا يكون للنوع ولا يثنى ولا يجمع، فهذا يدل دلالة واضحة على أن المصدر المأخوذ في الفعل لا يصلح دالاً على الوحدة أو التعدد، وإلا لجاز تأكيده بما يكون للنوع أو العدد وهو المثنى أو المجموع فافهم، وأيضاً قد بينا أن تقدير المفعول خلاف الظاهر لا يعتبر بدون قرينة دالة على تعينه فتدبر وأحسن التدبر، وإن الحق لا يتجاوز عما عليه مشايخنا الكرام .
Because it is necessary in usage, it is not valid to interpret it as a specific term because it is restricted and not indicated by any of the indications, and there is no contextual indicator against it. So it is also not permissible. It might be said that the Shafi'is say that estimation is necessary because the object is a necessary concomitant of the verb, so they are not content with 'eating' being absolute but rather prohibit it. And if it is said: 'The specificity of "I do not eat" customarily indicates the negation of absolute eating,' it is said: 'If this is granted, then there is no discussion about the specificity of this act, and its refutation is apparent, because the restriction by the object is not in the wording, so a contextual indicator must be added to indicate it and its specificity, and there is none, since the discussion is about something without a contextual indicator for the estimation of the object. As for the verb being transitive, it does not serve as a contextual indicator, as it was stated that it often takes the place of an intransitive verb. And if no contextual indicator is established for the restriction by the object, the verb remains absolute, and the absolute does not indicate the particular in any way. So understand.' (And) Sheikh Ibn al-Hajib objected to the absoluteness (i.e., the absoluteness of the verb) because of the impossibility of the existence of the universal natural entity externally, so the absolute does not exist. (This is rebutted) by what is established in its place: derived words indicate the nature as such, and the existence or non-existence of the universal natural entity has no bearing on it, so absoluteness is established and there is no room for objection. (And) by what is verified of the existence of the universal natural entity by the very existence of individuals, and what is meant is the nature as such, not the nature in terms of absoluteness that would contradict existence, as claimed. The Shafi'is said: 'I do not eat' is like 'I do not eat an eating,' and the second accepts specification by agreement, so does the first. We say: The similarity is denied, and 'an eating' indicates an individual because it is a source with tanwin, and it is for the dispersed individual, so if it is interpreted as a specific individual, it is accepted. As for the verb, it is for the truth as such without indicating individuality, so interpreting it by some individuals without others is not accepted. So ponder. For if it is said: The source with tanwin is also absolute, so it is not permissible to interpret it as a specific individual, like the source understood in the verb. Also, the source is emphatic, so the meaning understood in the verb and the meaning of the explicit source are one. I say: The source understood in the verb in itself is not permissible to be restricted because of the lack of indication of individuality; the one with tanwin indicates individuality, and sometimes absolute individuality is meant (which is literal), and sometimes a specific individual is meant (which is metaphorical). And being for emphasis is not obligatory in it; rather it may be for indicating the type or number, so it is permissible to intend a specific type or specific number. As for the source understood in the verb, it is not suitable to intend any individual at all, because individuality contradicts derivation from it. For if you say: Did not the scholars of rhetoric say that the verb has a subordinate metaphor, and that is nothing but a manipulation of the source understood in the verb? And you have refused here to intend the restricted from the mentioned source? The answer is: We do not deny figurative usage in the source from which it is derived, so that the verb may be used figuratively accordingly. We only deny the restriction of the source understood in the verb, because the restricted is not suitable to be derived from it, and it is not suitable for attribution to many entities as is the case with the derived word. The subordinate metaphor is the first, and the prohibited is the second. So contemplate. Then they said: According to this, it would follow that intending travel in 'he does not go out' and intending three divorces in 'you are irrevocably divorced' is not valid. He answered by saying: 'I say: Know that some natures are ambiguous (mushakkak), so they are more intense in some and weaker in others. Thus, in its essence, it is variegated, accepts division, and rulings differ. So if one intends a degree of its degrees, it is valid figuratively, like going out for travel and otherwise, for it is ambiguous in both, so intending travel from going out is valid. And divorce is light and heavy, so intending one of the two types is valid. So understand.' And in it there is something, for the univocal is like the ambiguous. The third chapter on linguistic principles. Intending some individuals? This ruling, because the relation of individuals to the univocal is like its relation to the ambiguous. Just as degrees from the ambiguous are valid figuratively, similarly it is valid in the univocal. So there is no difference between 'I do not eat' and 'he goes out'. So the truth is that it should be said: The individual resulting from restriction by the object is not permissible to be intended in 'I eat', so it is not permissible to intend 'I eat an apple' or 'bread', because the restriction by the object is not observed by the speaker due to its being omitted and forgotten. Similarly, it is not permissible to intend these individuals from 'going out' in 'he does not go out', so going out to Kufa or Basra is not intended. Rather, what is permissible is to intend some types, for it is a manipulation in the spoken expression, for they are individuals not with respect to the object. And it is not permissible to intend individuals of eating while disregarding restriction by the object eaten as well, because its reality is only a specific movement of the living, and these specificities of this movement are not customarily intended. And the discussion here is not about intending these individuals, unlike when the source is explicit, for it is a source with tanwin, and it may be for indicating the type, so it is permissible to consider variety according to restriction by the eaten object. But in 'I do not eat', there is no source for variety. Do you not see that grammarians are unanimous that the emphatic source is not for type, and is not dualized or pluralized? This clearly indicates that the source taken in the verb is not suitable to indicate unity or multiplicity, otherwise it would be permissible to emphasize it with what is for type or number, i.e., the dual or plural. So understand. Also, we have shown that estimating the object is contrary to the apparent meaning and is not considered without a contextual indicator indicating its specificity. So contemplate and reflect well. And the truth does not exceed what our noble scholars have held.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul dispute about the interpretation of verbs like 'لا آكل' (I do not eat). The author refutes the Shafi'i view that such verbs can be taken to imply a specific object (like 'I do not eat apples') by analogy to explicit masdars with tanwin. The Hanafi position is that the implicit masdar in the verb indicates the essence of the act, not any individual instance; therefore, without a contextual indicator (qarina), the verb remains absolute (mutlaq) and cannot be restricted. The author also addresses Ibn al-Hajib's objection about the universal natural entity, clarifying that derived words denote the nature as such regardless of external existence. Furthermore, the discussion extends to ambiguous (mushakkak) and univocal (mutawati') natures, showing that intending specific types (like travel from 'going out') is valid figuratively. The conclusion reiterates the Hanafi stance: the truth is with our noble scholars.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): A term that conveys the essence without any restriction or qualification.
مصدر منون (masdar munawwan): A verbal noun with nunation, indicating a specific or dispersed individual, type, or number.
قرينة (qarina): A contextual indicator that clarifies the intended meaning, such as a specific object or circumstance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul as argued in the passage, why cannot the verb in 'لا آكل' be interpreted to mean 'I do not eat apples'?
A) Because the verb is intransitive and cannot take an object.
B) Because the verb indicates only the essence of eating, not any particular object.
C) Because apples are not mentioned in the verb.
D) Because the Shafi'is disagree with that interpretation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a verb without a qarina remains mutlaq and cannot be specified to a particular object; the implicit masdar denotes essence, not individuals.

Rational Specification (Takhsis) of the General: The Case of 'La Yastawi'
Usul dispute on the scope of a general Qur'anic negation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that rational necessity ('aql) can serve as a qarina (contextual indicator) to specify a general Qur'anic text, using the example of Q. 59:20.

Core Idea
Absolute negation of equality is impossible; 'aql specifies the verse to the afterlife.

This passage examines the interpretation of the verse 'The companions of the Fire are not equal to the companions of Paradise.' At first glance, it appears to be a general negation. However, Hanafi usul scholars argue that since all things share the attribute of existence, absolute equality in every respect is rationally impossible. Therefore, the intellect ('aql) acts as a qarina to restrict the negation to the afterlife. This illustrates the concept of 'amm makhsus (general but specified) and the role of rational reasoning in textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the apparent generality
The verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة' negates equality without any explicit qualification. Taken at face value, it appears to deny all forms of equality between the two groups.
This is the initial textual reading that leads to the dispute.
2
Identify the rational impossibility
Absolute negation of equality is logically false because every two things share at least the attribute of existence (and thingness). Thus, the literal generality cannot be intended.
Hanafis use 'aql (intellect) to recognise this impossibility.
3
Apply the principle: 'aql as qarina
Since the literal meaning is impossible, the intellect provides a contextual indicator (qarina 'aqliyya) that restricts the negation to a specific respect – here, the afterlife and its rewards and punishments.
This is the Hanafi method of takhsis using rational necessity.
4
Contrast with unconditional negation
Unlike the statement 'لا آكل' (I do not eat), where no rational impossibility compels restriction, the verse cannot be left unrestricted. The 'aql forces a specification, whereas in 'لا آكل' the context (ordinary speech) allows the absolute negation.
The Shafi'i analogy to 'لا آكل' is rejected because the qarina is absent there.
5
Determine the specific scope
After restricting by 'aql, the question remains: to what exactly does the negation apply? Imam Abu Hanifa holds it applies specifically to the afterlife (akhirah) and its rulings (reward and punishment). Other scholars disagree on the scope but accept the necessity of specification.
The dispute is only after takhsis; all agree the verse is 'amm makhsus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (الاستواء بين (الشيئين أياً كان الشيئان بوجه ما معلوم (الصدق) فإن كان شيئين متشاركان في وصف، وأقله الشيئية والوجود وسلب الاستواء مطلقاً من جميع الوجوه (معلوم البطلان) لتحقق نقيضه الذي هو الاستواء بوجه ما (فلا يفيد الأول ولا يصدق الثاني إلا) لكن يفيد ثبوت الاستواء ويصدق سلبه ببعض الوجوه المعينة (فقوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَوِيَ أَصْحَبُ النَّارِ وَأَصْحَبُ الْجَنَّةِ أَصْحَبُ الْجَنَّةِ هُمُ الْفَابِرُونَ ) [الحشر: ۲۰] (الآية عام مخصوص لا مخالفة فيه كما ظن في شرح المختصر وغيره وكيف يجوز عاقل عموم سلب الاستواء من جميع الوجوه، ولذا قيل في بعض شروح المنهاج : إن المراد عمومه فيما يصح فيه العموم، بهذا قد دريت سقوط ما قيل في تأييد قول الشافعي وإثبات العموم وإلزام الحنفية بأن لا يستوي، ورد فيه النفي على مطلق الاستواء، إذ لا تقييد فيه، فلا يصح تقييده بمتعلق من المتعلقات، ولا يصح تخصيصه أيضاً بالأحكام الأخروية، وصار مثل : لا آكل : وذلك لأن نفي المطلق غير معقول يصح عمومه أصلاً، فضلاً عن أن يذهب إليه ذاهب فالعقل ههنا قرينة التقييد بالمتعلق، فليس مثل لا آكل فإنا لا نمنع التقييد، وجواز التخصيص فيما لا يكون فيه قرينة دالة على التقييد صارفة عن الإطلاق، فلا بد من تقدير المتعلق في لا يستوي وتعلق لحاظ المتكلم إليه، والمقدر كالملفوظ فيصح تخصيصه فافهم وإنما النزاع أن عمومه بعدما خصص) بما يصح (هل يخص الآخرة وأحكامها من الثواب والعقاب (كما هو رأي الإمام أبي حنيفة، فيقتل ولا
Question: Equality between two things, whatever the two things may be, in some respect is known to be true. For if two things share in a description, the least of which is thingness and existence, then negating equality absolutely from all respects is known to be false, because its opposite, which is equality in some respect, is realized. So the first (i.e., absolute negation of equality) is not useful, and the second is not true except that it affirms the establishment of equality and its negation is true in some specific respects. So His statement, the Exalted: 'The companions of the Fire are not equal to the companions of Paradise; the companions of Paradise are the successful' [Qur'an 59:20] is a general text that is specified. There is no disagreement in this, as was thought in Sharh al-Mukhtasar and elsewhere. For how can a rational person permit a general negation of equality from all respects? Hence it was said in some commentaries of al-Minhaj: 'What is meant is its generality in what generality is valid for.' By this you have come to know the downfall of what was said in support of the Shafi'i's statement and the establishment of generality and the imposition upon the Hanafis that 'they are not equal', and that the negation is applied to absolute equality, since there is no restriction in it. So it is not valid to restrict it to any of the things it may be related to, nor is it valid to specify it with the afterlife rulings. And it becomes like 'I do not eat'. This is because the negation of the absolute is not rationally valid for its generality at all, let alone that someone would go to it. But here the intellect is a contextual indicator for restriction to the related thing, so it is not like 'I do not eat'. For we do not forbid restriction and the permissibility of specification in cases where there is no contextual indicator indicating restriction that diverts from absoluteness. So estimation of the related thing in 'they are not equal' is necessary, and the speaker's attention is linked to it, and the estimated is like the uttered, so specification is valid. So understand. The dispute is only that after it is specified with what is valid, does it specifically refer to the afterlife and its rulings of reward and punishment, as is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa? ... (cuts off)
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage addresses the interpretation of the Qur'anic verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة' (The companions of the Fire are not equal to the companions of Paradise). The author argues that absolute negation of equality is rationally impossible because all things share at least the attributes of thingness and existence. Therefore, the negation must be restricted to certain aspects. The Hanafi position is that the 'aql (intellect) provides a contextual indicator (qarina) that restricts the meaning to the afterlife and its rewards and punishments, as held by Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage criticizes the Shafi'i view that the verse is unqualified and applies to all aspects of equality. The author emphasizes that this verse is an example of 'amm makhsus (general but restricted) and that the intellect serves as a qarina for that restriction, unlike the case of 'لا آكل' where there is no such qarina.

Key Terms
عام مخصوص (amm makhsus): A general term that is nevertheless intended to apply only to a subset of its potential referents, due to a contextual indicator or rational necessity.
استواء (istiswa'): Equality or sameness in some attribute; the verse negates it in a qualified sense.
قرينة عقلية (qarina 'aqliyya): A rational contextual indicator that restricts an otherwise general or absolute statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best represents the Hanafi position on the verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة'?
A) It absolutely negates all equality between the two groups.
B) It is a general statement but restricted by rational necessity to equality in the afterlife.
C) It only negates equality in worldly status.
D) It indicates that the two groups are equal in some respects and unequal in others.

Key Takeaway
Rational impossibility forces specification of a general text; the intellect ('aql) is a valid qarina for takhsis in Hanafi usul.

Intending Particular Individuals from General Negation: A Hanafi Linguistic Analysis
Ruling on the impossibility of intending specific individuals from general negation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a general negative verb like 'لا آكل' cannot be interpreted to refer to a specific object without a contextual indicator, and apply this principle to new examples.

Core Idea
A general negation remains general; the omitted object is not intended unless a clear context specifies it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explores a subtle linguistic principle: when someone says 'I do not eat,' can we assume they mean 'I do not eat apples'? The Hanafi position, grounded in the nature of univocal terms and grammatical structure, says no. The speaker's omission of the object is deliberate and forgotten, so the negation applies to the act itself, not any particular instance. We'll unpack the reasoning and its implications for legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What is the legal question? Can a general negation be interpreted to refer to specific individuals? The passage addresses this through the examples 'لا آكل' and 'لا يخرج'.
2
Understand key terms
What are متواطىء (univocal) and مشكك (ambiguous)? The author argues that the relationship of individuals to the univocal term is like that to the ambiguous term, so levels are permissible metaphorically. How does this support the ruling?
Univocal terms apply equally, ambiguous terms apply with gradation.
3
Analyze the verb construction
In 'آكل', the object is omitted and forgotten. The speaker does not intend a specific object like 'apple' or 'bread'. This is key: the restriction with an object is not considered because the object is absent. Similarly for 'يخرج'.
The omission is deliberate; the verb alone conveys the general act.
4
Examine the grammatical argument
The author uses a grammatical point: the verbal noun (مصدر) in the verb cannot indicate type or number, as grammarians agree that the emphasized verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized. This shows the verb's المصدر is not suitable for specifying individuals.
If it could indicate type, it would be allowed to emphasize it with dual/plural forms, but it is not.
5
Apply the ruling
How does this principle apply? 'لا يخرج' does not mean 'he does not go out to Kufa or Basra'. It remains general. Only an explicit contextual indicator (قرينة) can specify. The author concludes by affirming this is the position of the Hanafi mashayikh.
The object is not in the speaker's intention; it is 'نسياً منسياً' (forgotten, overlooked).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية في إرادة بعض هذا الحكم، لأن نسبة الأفراد إلى المتواطىء كنسبتها إلى المشكك، فكما يصح المراتب من المشكك تجوزاً، كذلك يجوز في المتواطىء، فلا فرق بين لا آكل وبين يخرج، فالحق إذن أن يقال : إن الفرد الحاصل من التقييد بالمفعول لا يجوز إرادتها في آكل، فلا يجوز إرادة آكل تفاحة أو خبزاً، فإن التقييد بالمفعول غير ملحوظ للمتكلم لكونه محذوفاً نسياً منسياً، وكذا لا يجوز إرادة هذه الأفراد من الخروج في لا يخرج فلا يراد الخروج إلى كوفة أو بصرة، وإنما يجوز فيه إرادة بعض الأنواع فإنه تصرف في المنطوق فإنها أفراد لا بالنسبة إلى المفعول، ولا يجوز أن يراد أفراد الأكل مع قطع النظر عن التقييد بمأكول أيضاً، لأن حقيقته ليست إلا حركة خاصة للحيين ولا يراد خصوصيات هذه الحركة عرفاً، وليس الكلام ههنا في إرادة هذه الإفراد بخلاف ما إذا صرح بالمصدر فإنه مصدر منون وهو قد يكون لبيان النوع، فيجوز أن يعتبر التنوع باعتبار التقييد بالمفعول المأكول وإما لا آكل فليس فيه المصدر للتنويع ، ألا ترى أن النحاة أجمعوا على أن المصدر المؤكد لا يكون للنوع ولا يثنى ولا يجمع، فهذا يدل دلالة واضحة على أن المصدر المأخوذ في الفعل لا يصلح دالاً على الوحدة أو التعدد، وإلا لجاز تأكيده بما يكون للنوع أو العدد وهو المثنى أو المجموع فافهم، وأيضاً قد بينا أن تقدير المفعول خلاف الظاهر لا يعتبر بدون قرينة دالة على تعينه فتدبر وأحسن التدبر، وإن الحق لا يتجاوز عما عليه مشايخنا الكرام .
The third article on linguistic principles. Regarding intending some of this ruling: because the relationship of individuals to the univocal term is like their relationship to the ambiguous term. Just as levels are valid from the ambiguous term metaphorically, similarly it is valid in the univocal term. So there is no difference between 'I do not eat' and 'he does not go out'. The truth therefore is that it should be said: The individual obtained by restriction with an object cannot be intended in 'eat', so it is not permissible to intend 'eat an apple' or 'eat bread', because the restriction with the object is not considered by the speaker since it is omitted, forgotten, overlooked. Likewise, it is not permissible to intend these individuals from 'going out' in 'he does not go out', so 'going out to Kufa or Basra' is not intended. Rather, it is permissible to intend some types, for that is a manipulation in the spoken form, for they are individuals not in relation to the object. And it is not permissible that the individuals of eating be intended while disregarding restriction with something eaten, because its reality is only a specific movement for the two living beings, and the particularities of this movement are not conventionally intended. And the discussion here is not about intending these individuals, unlike when the verbal noun is explicitly mentioned, for it is a nunated verbal noun and it may be to indicate the type, so diversity may be considered in terms of restriction with the object eaten. But as for 'I do not eat', it does not contain the verbal noun for diversification. Do you not see that the grammarians have agreed that the emphasized verbal noun is not for the type, nor is it dualized or pluralized? This is clear evidence that the verbal noun taken in the verb cannot indicate unity or plurality; otherwise it would be permissible to emphasize it with that which is for type or number, which is the dual or plural. So understand. And also we have shown that estimating the object is contrary to the apparent and is not considered without a contextual indicator indicating its specificity. So deliberate and deliberate well. And the truth does not go beyond what our noble masters (mashayikh) have held.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the third article on linguistic principles. The author discusses the scope of general negation in verbs like 'لا آكل' (I do not eat) and 'لا يخرج' (he does not go out). He argues that these general terms cannot be interpreted to refer to specific individuals (like eating a specific fruit or going to a specific city) unless there is an explicit contextual indicator. The key point is that the object in such constructions is omitted and forgotten, so the speaker does not intend a particular object. The reasoning is based on the nature of univocal (متواطىء) and ambiguous (مشكك) terms. The author also uses a grammatical argument: the verbal noun derived from the verb cannot indicate type or number, as grammarians agree that the emphasized verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized. This shows that the verb's verbal noun is not suitable to convey specific individuals. Therefore, the ruling is that general negation remains general unless there is a clear context to specify it. The author concludes by affirming that this is the position of the Hanafi mashayikh.

Key Terms
المتواطىء (al-mutawati'): A univocal term that applies equally to all its individuals without gradation, like 'animal' applying equally to humans and horses.
المشكك (al-mushakkak): An ambiguous term that applies to its individuals with gradation, like 'existence' which applies to substances and accidents in different degrees.
المصدر المؤكد (al-masdar al-mu'akkad): The emphasized verbal noun (e.g., 'أكلت أكلاً') that is used to confirm the action, not to indicate type or number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the verbal noun in the verb cannot indicate type or number?
A) Because it is always emphasized.
B) Because grammarians agree that the emphasized verbal noun is not dualized or pluralized.
C) Because it is derived from an intransitive verb.
D) Because the verb is in the past tense.

Key Takeaway
A general negation like 'لا آكل' cannot be restricted to specific objects without an explicit contextual indicator; the Hanafi school relies on linguistic and grammatical proofs to maintain generality.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Scope of a Specified General Verse: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Q.59:20
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on the scope of Quranic verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a general text ('amm) can be specified (takhsis) by context, and evaluate how this affects the conflict between two general Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The verse 'لا يستوي' is specified to the Hereafter, so it does not contradict the general retribution verses.

In this lesson, we examine a classical usul dispute over the scope of the Quranic verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة'. The Hanafis hold that this verse, though general in wording, is specified by its context to only matters of the Hereafter. This specification allows another set of general verses (on qisas) to remain operative, leading to the ruling that a Muslim can be killed for a dhimmi. The Shafi'i position, on the other hand, maintains that the verse retains its generality in both worlds, and thus conflicts with the qisas verses, preventing such retribution. We will trace the arguments and understand the usul principle behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Text and Its Category
Locate the verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة' in the source. Recognize that it is a general ('amm) text but agreed to be specified (makhsus) by some evidence.
The specification is not disputed; the dispute is on the scope after specification.
2
State the Point of Dispute
After specification, does the verse apply to this world and the Hereafter, or only to the Hereafter? This is the core disagreement.
3
Outline the Hanafi Proof
The Hanafi position relies on the context within the verse itself ('أصحاب الجنة هم الفائزون') which refers to Hereafter success, and the imperceptibility of one's final abode.
This restricts the verse to Hereafter matters.
4
Outline the Shafi'i Proof
The Shafi'i position argues that the negation 'لا يستوي' is absolute without restriction, so it should apply to all rulings.
They treat the verse as retaining its full generality.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response shows that absolute negation is impossible (two things always share some aspect), and the context provides a natural restriction. Therefore, the verse does not conflict with the general retribution verses.
The retribution verses remain operative, allowing a Muslim to be killed for a dhimmi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (الاستواء بين (الشيئين أياً كان الشيئان بوجه ما معلوم (الصدق) فإن كان شيئين متشاركان في وصف، وأقله الشيئية والوجود وسلب الاستواء مطلقاً من جميع الوجوه (معلوم البطلان) لتحقق نقيضه الذي هو الاستواء بوجه ما (فلا يفيد الأول ولا يصدق الثاني إلا) لكن يفيد ثبوت الاستواء ويصدق سلبه ببعض الوجوه المعينة (فقوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَوِيَ أَصْحَبُ النَّارِ وَأَصْحَبُ الْجَنَّةِ أَصْحَبُ الْجَنَّةِ هُمُ الْفَابِرُونَ ) [الحشر: ۲۰] (الآية عام مخصوص لا مخالفة فيه كما ظن في شرح المختصر وغيره وكيف يجوز عاقل عموم سلب الاستواء من جميع الوجوه، ولذا قيل في بعض شروح المنهاج : إن المراد عمومه فيما يصح فيه العموم، بهذا قد دريت سقوط ما قيل في تأييد قول الشافعي وإثبات العموم وإلزام الحنفية بأن لا يستوي، ورد فيه النفي على مطلق الاستواء، إذ لا تقييد فيه، فلا يصح تقييده بمتعلق من المتعلقات، ولا يصح تخصيصه أيضاً بالأحكام الأخروية، وصار مثل : لا آكل : وذلك لأن نفي المطلق غير معقول يصح عمومه أصلاً، فضلاً عن أن يذهب إليه ذاهب فالعقل ههنا قرينة التقييد بالمتعلق، فليس مثل لا آكل فإنا لا نمنع التقييد، وجواز التخصيص فيما لا يكون فيه قرينة دالة على التقييد صارفة عن الإطلاق، فلا بد من تقدير المتعلق في لا يستوي وتعلق لحاظ المتكلم إليه، والمقدر كالملفوظ فيصح تخصيصه فافهم وإنما النزاع أن عمومه بعدما خصص) بما يصح (هل يخص الآخرة وأحكامها من الثواب والعقاب (كما هو رأي الإمام أبي حنيفة، فيقتل المسلم بالذمي لعموم آيات القصاص من غير معارضتها هذه الآية وتلك الآيات، مثل قوله تعالى : الحُرُّ بِالْحَرِ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۷۸] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَكُمْ فِي الْقِصَاصِ حَيَوةٌ يَتأُولِي الْأَلْبَابِ [البقرة : ١٧٩] وقوله : النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْس [المائدة: ٤٥] (أو) أن عمومه بعدما خصص (يعم الدارين) من الأحكام (كما ذهب إليه الإمام الشافعي: فلا يقتل المسلم بالذمي عنده المعارضة الآيات الدالة على وجوب القصاص مع هذه الآية ولا حجية مع قيام المعارضة (والظاهر مع) الإمام أبي حنيفة لقوله تعالى في سياقها (أصحاب الجنة هم الفائزون) ولا شك أن المراد الفوز الأخروي ولأن كون صاحب الجنة أو صاحب النار مما لا يدرك، فإنه موقوف على الخاتمة، وذلك مما لا يدرك أصلاً، فلا يدخل تحت حكم القاضي أنه من أهل الجنة، فلا يقتل بمن هو من أهل النار ، وإرادة الكافر ظاهراً من أهل النار والمؤمن ظاهراً من أهل الجنة الفائزون ( ولحديث ابن البيلماني) بالباء الموحدة واللام المفتوحتين بينهما ياء ساكنة من التابعين ذكره ابن حبان في الثقات وضعفه الدارقطني كذا في «التيسير» قتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مسلماً بمعاهد وقال : أنا أحق بوفاء ذمته رواه أبو داود وعبد الرزاق والدارقطني عن ابن البيلماني عن ابن عمر مرفوعاً ، كذا في «التيسير» (ولقول) أمير المؤمنين (علي رضي الله تعالى عنه : إنما بذلوا الجزية لتكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا، قال الشيخ ابن الهمام في فتح القدير: لم يجده المخرجون بهذا اللفظ، وروى الشافعي من طريق الإمام محمد بسند فيه أبو الجنوب : من كان له ذمة فدمه كدمنا وديته كديتنا، وقال أبو الجنوب : ضعيف وفي التيسير رواه الدارقطني أيضاً بسند فيه أبو الجنوب، ثم إن قول أمير المؤمنين يحتمل أن يكون وجه الشبه نفس حرمة الدم لا وجوب القصاص، فلا يصلح حجة، والذي ورد في الصحاح من قول أمير المؤمنين : لا يقتل مسلم بكافر، وهذا لو لم يخص دل على عدم اقتصاص المسلم بالذمي لكن الحق قول الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، فإن النصوص القرآنية العامة لا يعارضها قول أحد، كما لا يخفى .
Issue: Equality between two things, whatever the two things may be, with respect to some aspect is known (true). If there are two things sharing a description, the minimum of which is thingness and existence, and absolute negation of equality from all aspects is known (false) due to the realization of its opposite, which is equality in some aspect. So the first (i.e., absolute equality) is not established, and the second (i.e., absolute negation) is not true, except that it establishes some equality and its negation is true in specific aspects. Thus His statement, the Exalted: “Not equal are the companions of the Fire and the companions of Paradise; the companions of Paradise – they are the attainers [of success]” (59:20) is a general text that has been specified; there is no disagreement in that, as some imagined in Sharh al-Mukhtasar and elsewhere. How could a rational person allow the generalization of the negation of equality from all aspects? Hence it was said in some commentaries of al-Minhaj: The intended meaning is its generality within what is valid for generality. By this you have come to know the fallacy of what was said in support of al-Shafi'i's view and proving generality and making it binding upon the Hanafis that [the verse] 'do not equate' negates absolute equality, since there is no restriction in it, so it is not valid to restrict it to any particular context, nor is it valid to specify it with worldly rulings. And it becomes like 'I do not eat'? This is because the negation of the absolute is unintelligible for its generality to be valid at all, let alone that someone should adopt it. But here reason is an indicator of restriction with context? It is not like 'I do not eat', for we do not prevent restriction, and permissibility of specification in what has no indicator of restriction that turns away from absoluteness. So it is necessary to estimate the context in 'do not equate' and the speaker's attention is attached to it, and the estimated is like the spoken, so its specification is valid. Understand. But the dispute is whether its generality after being specified (with what is valid) applies exclusively to the Hereafter and its rulings of reward and punishment (as is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa), so that a Muslim may be killed for a dhimmi due to the generality of the verses of retribution, with no conflict between these verses and that [verse]? Examples include His statement: “The free for the free” (2:178), “And there is for you in legal retribution [saving of] life” (2:179), and “The soul for the soul” (5:45). Or that its generality after specification applies to both abodes of rulings (as al-Shafi'i held), so that a Muslim is not killed for a dhimmi in his view, due to the conflict with the verses indicating the obligation of retribution along with this verse, and there is no authority when conflict exists. And the apparent view is with Imam Abu Hanifa due to His statement in its context: “The companions of Paradise – they are the attainers [of success].” There is no doubt that the intended is the success of the Hereafter, and because being a companion of Paradise or a companion of the Fire is imperceptible; it depends on the final outcome, and that is not perceptible at all. So it does not come under the judge's ruling that someone is among the people of Paradise, so he is not killed for someone who is among the people of Fire. And the apparent intent is that the disbeliever is of the people of Fire and the apparent believer is of the people of Paradise, the attainers. And due to the hadith of Ibn al-Bilamani – with a ba with one dot and two open lams with a silent ya between them, from the Followers, mentioned by Ibn Hibban in al-Thiqat and declared weak by al-Daraqutni, as in al-Taysir – that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, killed a Muslim for a mu'ahid (protected person) and said: “I am the most entitled to fulfill his covenant.” Narrated by Abu Dawud, Abd al-Razzaq, and al-Daraqutni from Ibn al-Bilamani from Ibn Umar marfu'an, as in al-Taysir. And due to the saying of the Commander of the Faithful, Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: “They paid jizya so that their blood would be like our blood and their wealth like our wealth.” Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: The [hadith] scholars did not find it with this wording. Al-Shafi'i narrated from the path of Imam Muhammad with a chain containing Abu al-Janub: “Whoever has a covenant, his blood is like our blood and his blood-money like our blood-money.” And Abu al-Janub is weak. In al-Taysir, al-Daraqutni also narrated it with a chain containing Abu al-Janub. Then, the saying of the Commander of the Faithful may be interpreted as the similarity being in the sanctity of blood itself, not the obligation of retribution, so it is not valid as evidence. And what is reported in the authentic collections from the saying of the Commander of the Faithful: “A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever.” This, if not specified, indicates that a Muslim is not subject to retribution for a dhimmi. But the truth is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, for the general Quranic texts are not contradicted by the saying of anyone, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (mas'ala) concerning the scope of the Quranic verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة' (Not equal are the companions of the Fire and the companions of Paradise). The author first establishes a linguistic principle: absolute equality or absolute inequality between two things in all aspects is impossible; rather, some equality always exists. The verse is thus a general text ('amm) that has been specified – a point agreed upon. The dispute arises after specification: does the verse apply only to the Hereafter (Hanafi view) or to both this world and the Hereafter (Shafi'i view)? The Hanafi position is that the verse refers exclusively to Hereafter matters, as indicated by the context 'أصحاب الجنة هم الفائزون' (the companions of Paradise are the attainers) which refers to success in the Hereafter. Therefore, the verse does not conflict with other general verses of retribution (like those in Surah al-Baqarah and al-Ma'idah) that allow killing a Muslim for a dhimmi. The Shafi'i view holds that the verse applies generally to all rulings, including worldly ones, so it conflicts with the retribution verses, and thus a Muslim cannot be killed for a dhimmi. The author supports Abu Hanifa's view, providing additional proofs: a hadith (though weak) where the Prophet killed a Muslim for a mu'ahid, and a saying of Ali that implies equality of blood. However, the author notes that these narrations are weak or can be interpreted differently. The ultimate argument is that general Quranic texts (the retribution verses) are not contradicted by a single verse that is specified to the Hereafter, nor by individual sayings. Thus, the Hanafi ruling that a Muslim can be killed for a dhimmi stands.

Key Terms
عام مخصوص ('amm makhsus): A general text that has been specified (by evidence), thus not all its individuals are intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what is the scope of the verse 'لا يستوي أصحاب النار وأصحاب الجنة'?
A) It applies to this world and the Hereafter equally.
B) It applies only to matters of the Hereafter.
C) It applies only to worldly matters.
D) It has no application after specification.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that the verse is specified to the Hereafter allows the general retribution verses to remain operative, supporting the ruling that a Muslim may be killed for a dhimmi.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Scope of Non-Independent Answers in Usul al-Fiqh
Dispute on non-independent answer scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a non-independent answer is specific to the question and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on tark al-istifsal.

Core Idea
A non-independent 'yes' stays within the question's specificity; the lack of clarification does not imply generality.

When someone asks a specific question and receives a simple 'yes', does that 'yes' apply only to that question or to all similar cases? This lesson unpacks a key usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. You will learn the Hanafi position that the answer is confined to the question's scope and why the Shafi'i appeal to 'tark al-istifsal' is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute concerns a non-independent answer (jawab ghayr mustaqill) like 'نعم' following a specific question. The questioner's context is key.
Non-independent means the answer cannot stand alone; it relies on the question.
2
State the Hanafi position
The preferred (al-awjah) Hanafi view: the answer equals the question in specificity; it does not generalize.
This is the view said to be unanimous among Hanafis according to some sources.
3
Present the Shafi'i argument
Shafi'is argue that since the Prophet (or narrator) did not seek clarification, the answer must be general; otherwise clarification would have been needed.
This is the argument from 'tark al-istifsal'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the questioner already understood the specific context, so there was no need for clarification. Therefore, tark al-istifsal cannot indicate generality.
The place does not require istifsal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a non-independent 'yes' to a specific question is limited to that question (Hanafi) versus applied generally (Shafi'i). This affects how we derive rulings from Prophetic answers.
Thus understanding this dispute helps in istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (جواب السائل) حال كون هذا الجواب (غير المستقل كنعم يساوي السؤال في العموم وفي الخصوص قيل كذلك أي يساويه في الخصوص أيضاً اتفاقاً (وهو الأوجه وقيل) في أكثر كتبنا : قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية ويدل عليه كلام الآمدي وبعض «شراح المختصر» لا اتفاق أصلاً بل (يعم) غير المستقل بعد السؤال الخاص (عند الشافعي لترك الاستفصال أي السائل أو الراوي لم يستفصله ولو كان خاصاً لاستفصل وفيه ما فيه فإنه ليس موضع الاستفصال ، لأن السائل إنما كان سأل عن أمر خاص وفهم جوابه فلا مساغ للاستفصال أصلاً ( وأما ) الجواب المستقل فإن كان مساوياً) للسؤال في العموم والخصوص (يتبع) ذلك الجواب السؤال كما هو ظاهر وإن كان الجواب خاصاً لا يعم إلا بالقياس) أو غيره من الدلائل (وإن كان الجواب عاماً وارداً على سبب خاص سؤال مثل قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم
Issue: The answer of the questioner, while this answer is non-independent like 'yes', equals the question in generality and specificity. It is said likewise, i.e., it equals it in specificity also unanimously – and that is the most plausible view. And it is said in most of our books: The author of Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya said, and supported by the statement of al-Amidi and some commentators of al-Mukhtasar, that there is no agreement at all, rather the non-independent answer is general after a specific question according to al-Shafi'i, due to the lack of seeking clarification (istifsal) – that is, the questioner or narrator did not seek clarification; if it were specific, he would have sought clarification. But there is something in this, for it is not a place for seeking clarification, because the questioner only asked about a specific matter and understood the answer, so there is no room for seeking clarification at all. As for the independent answer: if it equals the question in generality and specificity, that answer follows the question, as is apparent. If the answer is specific, it does not generalize except by analogy or other evidences. And if the answer is general coming upon a specific cause or question, like the saying of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace and his Companions peace...
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (mas'ala) about the scope of non-independent answers, such as 'نعم' (yes), when responding to a question. The core issue is whether such an answer shares the same scope (general or specific) as the question or whether it becomes general even if the question is specific. There are two views: The first view holds that the answer is identical in scope to the question, both in generality and specificity, and this is considered the most plausible (al-awjah). The second view, attributed to some Hanafi books and to al-Shafi'i, holds that there is no agreement; rather, a non-independent answer is general after a specific question. The justification for the second view is that the Prophet or the narrator did not seek clarification, implying that the answer is general. However, the author criticizes this reasoning, arguing that there is no need for clarification because the questioner asked about a specific matter and understood the answer accordingly. The passage then moves to independent answers (where the answer is a complete sentence). For independent answers, if they match the question in scope, they follow the question. If the independent answer is specific, it does not generalize except through analogy (qiyas) or other evidences. If the independent answer is general but comes in response to a specific cause (like a question), the text begins to give an example but cuts off. The author appears to favor the first view, that the non-independent answer is confined to the scope of the question.

Key Terms
جواب غير المستقل (jawab ghayr al-mustaqill): A non-independent answer, like 'yes' or 'no', that does not form a complete sentence and depends on the question for meaning.
ترك الاستفصال (tark al-istifsal): The omission of seeking clarification by the questioner or narrator; some use this as evidence that the answer is general.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, how does a non-independent answer like 'نعم' relate to the question's scope?
A) It always generalizes the question.
B) It equals the question in both generality and specificity.
C) It is always specific regardless of the question.
D) It is independent and has its own scope.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view that a non-independent answer is confined to the scope of the question is preferred because the questioner's understood context obviates the need for clarification.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
General Wording Governs Over Specific Cause
Establishing the usul principle that consideration is for the general wording, not the specific cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a general wording revealed for a specific cause remains general, and evaluate the Hanafi evidence against the contrary view.

Core Idea
General wording applies universally unless a specifier exists; the specific cause does not restrict it.

This passage from Sharh Musallam al-Thubut establishes a foundational usul rule: when a general text is revealed for a particular reason, the ruling is not limited to that reason. The author explains the majority view held by Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis, and responds to the minority position attributed to al-Shafi'i. By studying this lesson, you will understand the strong evidence from the practice of the Companions and the linguistic principle that general words carry their full scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its scope
The text states 'العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب'. Understand that this means the wording of a text applies to all cases, not just the specific occasion.
2
Classify the types of answers
The author distinguishes non-independent answers (like 'yes') that mirror the question, and independent answers. When an answer is independent and general but arises from a specific cause, the generality holds.
3
Examine the key evidence
Two hadith examples: the well of Buda'a ('water is pure') and the sheep of Maymuna ('any skin tanned is purified'). Note how the general wording is applied universally.
The well of Buda'a hadith is often cited as the prime example.
4
Analyze the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Some attribute to al-Shafi'i the view that the ruling is restricted to the cause. The author shows this is a mistake; al-Shafi'i himself said the opposite. Also note the practice of Companions as consensus.
Imam al-Shafi'i's al-Umm supports generality.
5
Apply the principle to Quranic verses
The verses of theft, zihar, and li'an were all revealed for specific incidents but are applied generally. This shows the principle in action.
Example: verse of theft revealed for a shield, yet applied to all theft.

Issue: Agreed. The answer of the questioner) while this answer is (non-independent like 'yes', it equals the question in generality and in specificity. (And if the answer is general, occurring on a specific cause of a question, like his saying, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, about the well of Buda'a) when a questioner asked about its water into which menstrual cloths were thrown: 'Indeed, water is pure; nothing makes it impure.' Narrated by Imam Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, and Abu Dawud. This example is valid only if the lām is not for the specific covenant, as some Hanafis said: the water of the well of Buda'a was flowing in gardens, and it is an indication in response to the deduction of Malik's followers using this hadith for the purity of all water. The detail is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir, Fath al-Mannan, and Sharh Safar al-Sa'ada. (Or) a specific cause other than a question, as it is narrated that) (he passed by a sheep of Maymuna and said: 'Any skin that is tanned is purified.') The hadith is authentic as in Fath al-Qadir and others, but it is not reported that it occurred concerning the sheep of Maymuna. What occurred concerning her is his saying: 'Why did you not make use of its skin?' They said: 'It is carrion.' He said: 'Only its eating is forbidden.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. According to the majority of Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis: (Consideration is for the generality of the wording, so it is acted upon, not for the specificity of the cause, unless the ruling is specified by it. (And) what is transmitted from al-Shafi'i is the opposite) i.e., consideration is for the specificity of the cause, not for the generality of the wording. It was said this is a mistake. And the author indicated its refutation by his saying: (And Imam al-Haramayn authenticated it, for he is more knowledgeable of his school. And in some commentaries of al-Minhaj, it is an error of the Imam. And al-Shafi'i explicitly stated in his book called al-Umm that the consideration is for the generality of the wording. And Imam al-Razi severely criticized those who attributed this statement to al-Shafi'i, and attributed it to Imam Malik, Abu Thawr, and al-Muzani. For us, firstly, the wording is general) placed for generality, so it must be acted upon unless there is a diverting factor, and no diverting factor can be imagined except its occurrence on a specific cause. (And the specificity of the cause does not qualify as a diverting factor) from what it was placed for, and (does not prevent acting upon it, as it requires, and this is apparent. (And) for us: (secondly, the adherence of the Companions and those after them) without objection to general statements occurring on specific causes, and this yields customary knowledge of consensus that the specificity of the cause does not prevent the generality of the wording. Such as (the verse of theft) they adhered to it, and it was revealed concerning the theft of a shield or the cloak of Safwan ibn Umayya as mentioned in some Tafsirs. And the verse of zihar) was revealed concerning Salama ibn Bayadi) — thus in the books of usul, while in hadith books, Salama pronounced zihar on his wife, so the Prophet ordered him to expiate. (Or) or Aws ibn al-Samit) — thus I found the copies of the text, and in hadith books it is with the letter sad: the story is that zihar was a divorce in the Jahiliyya, so Khawla, the wife of Aws ibn al-Samit, came to the Messenger of Allah and informed him, and Aws had said: 'I think she has become forbidden [؟]' as in al-Tabarani's narration. So she went to the Messenger of Allah and argued with him, then Allah revealed: {Indeed Allah has heard the statement of her who argues with you concerning her husband} (al-Mujadila 58:1). This is established in the Sahihs and Sunans. And the verse of li'an) was revealed concerning Hilal ibn Umayya) as in Sahih al-Bukhari and others. His story is that he found a partner with his wife, so he mentioned it to the Messenger of Allah, who said: 'Evidence or a hadd on your back.' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if one of us sees a man with his wife, he goes to seek evidence?' The Messenger of Allah repeated his statement. Then he said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth, I am truthful, and Allah will clear my back from the hadd.' So the verse of li'an was revealed. (Or) (Uwaymir) as in the two Sahihs and others too numerous to mention. Those who specify by the cause (said: Firstly, if what is revealed concerning a specific cause were general, it would be permissible to specify the cause) from it (by ijtihad) because its relation to it is like the relation of other individuals that may be specified by ijtihad, either absolutely or... (Ibn Sakhr?)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh discussion on the principle: Is consideration given to the general wording (عموم اللفظ) or to the specific cause (خصوص السبب) when a general statement is made in response to a specific question or situation? The text begins by categorizing answers: non-independent answers (like 'yes') that mirror the question in scope, and independent answers. It then addresses the case where an answer is general but arises from a specific cause. The majority of Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis hold that the generality of the wording governs, not the specific cause. The text provides examples: the hadith of the well of Buda'a (about water purity) and the hadith of the sheep of Maymuna (about tanning skins). It notes that even if a hadith is reported for a specific situation, its general wording applies. The author refutes the attribution to al-Shafi'i of the opposite view (consideration for the specific cause), citing that al-Shafi'i himself in al-Umm affirmed the generality principle. The passage then gives Quranic examples: the verse of theft (al-Ma'idah 5:38) revealed about a specific theft, the verse of zihar (al-Mujadila) revealed about a specific woman, and the verse of li'an (al-Nur 24:6-9) revealed about Hilal or Uwaymir. In all these cases, the Companions applied the general ruling, not restricting it to the specific cause. This proves that the specific cause does not limit the general wording. The Hanafis emphasize that the word 'عام' is placed for generality, and the specific cause is not a valid specifier. The principle is: العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب.

Key Terms
عموم اللفظ (ʿumūm al-lafẓ): The generality of the wording of a text, which applies to all individuals encompassed by its meaning.
خصوص السبب (khuṣūṣ al-sabab): The specific cause or occasion for the revelation of a text; it does not restrict the generality of the wording.
سبب (sabab): The specific event or question that prompted the revelation or utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis, what is the principle when a general wording comes for a specific cause?
A) The ruling is restricted to that specific cause.
B) The general wording applies to all cases unless specified by another evidence.
C) The ruling is cancelled due to the specific cause.
D) The specific cause overrides the generality.

Key Takeaway
A general text revealed for a specific cause retains its generality; the specific cause does not restrict the ruling.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Generality of Wording vs. Specific Occasion
Usul dispute on the scope of general texts revealed on specific occasions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that generality of wording governs by deriving rulings from general texts revealed on specific occasions, and evaluate the counter-argument regarding ijtihad-based exclusion.

Core Idea
A specific cause does not restrict a general wording — the ruling applies to all cases.

The principle 'al-'ibra li'umum al-lafz la li'khusus al-sabab' is foundational in Hanafi usul. This lesson examines the dispute over whether a general text revealed on a specific occasion applies universally. The Hanafi position, shared by the majority, is that the general wording governs, not the specific cause. We will explore the proofs and the counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its proponents
State the principle 'al-'ibra li'umum al-lafz la li'khusus al-sabab'. Note that the majority of Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis affirm it. Recognize the opposing view attributed (incorrectly) to al-Shafi'i.
The author clarifies that al-Shafi'i himself affirmed the general rule in al-Umm.
2
Analyze the first proof: linguistic nature of generality
The wording is placed for generality; a specific cause is not a valid preventer (sarf) from acting upon the general meaning. Understand that the default is to apply the general wording unless a clear preventer exists.
This proof relies on the primacy of linguistic function.
3
Analyze the second proof: practice of the Companions
The Companions applied general verses that were revealed on specific occasions (e.g., theft verse, zihar verse, li'an verse) without restricting them. This yields customary knowledge of consensus (ijma).
This demonstrates that the specific cause does not prevent generality.
4
Evaluate the objection and Hanafi response
The objectors argue that if the wording is general, one could exclude the specific cause by ijtihad, like other individuals. The Hanafi response: the specific cause is definitively included because the wording is an answer (jawaab) to a question, and correspondence (mutabaqah) is obligatory. Thus, it cannot be excluded.
The answer's correspondence with the question is a contextual indication (qarinah) of definite inclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية في بئر بضاعة) حين سأل سائل عن مائها يلقى فيه ثياب الحيض: إن الماء طهور لا ينجسه شيء) رواه الإمام أحمد والترمذي وأبو داود وهذا المثال إنما يصح لو لم تكن اللام للعهد كما قاله بعض الحنفية إن ماء بئر بضاعة كان جارياً في البساتين وهو إشارة إليه في جواب استدلال أصحاب مالك بهذا الحديث على طهارة كل ماء، والتفصيل مذكور في «فتح القدير» و«فتح المنان» و«شرح سفر السعادة (أو) سبب خاص غير سؤال كما روي أنه) (مر بشاة ميمونة فقال : أيما إهاب دبغ فقد طهر) الحديث صحيح كما في فتح القدير» وغيره لكن لم ينقل وقوعه في شاة ميمونة والذي وقع فيها قوله الله الله الهلال انتفعتم بإهابها فقالوا : إنها ميتة، فقال: إنما حرم أكلها» رواه الشيخان فعند الأكثر من الحنفية والشافعية والمالكية (العبرة لعموم اللفظ فيعمل به لا لخصوص السبب حتى يخص الحكم به (و) المروي عن الشافعي بالعكس) أي العبرة لخصوص السبب لا لعموم اللفظ ، قيل هذا ،غلط، وأشار المصنف إلى رده بقوله : (وصححه إمام الحرمين فإنه أعرف بمذهبه، وفي بعض «شروح المنهاج» إنه خطأ الإمام، وصرح الشافعي في كتابه المسمى بالأم أن العبرة لعموم اللفظ، وشدد النكير الإمام الرازي على من نسب هذا القول إلى الشافعي ونسب فيه هذا القول إلى الإمام مالك وأبي ثور والمزني لنا أولاً اللفظ عام) موضوع للعموم فيجب العمل به إلا لصارف، ولا صارف يتخيل إلا وروده على سبب خاص (وخصوص السبب لا يصلح صارفاً إياه عما وضع بإزائه و(لا يمنع العمل به كما اقتضاه وهذا ظاهر (و) لنا :(ثانياً : تمسك الصحابة ومن بعدهم) من غير نكير بالعمومات الواردة على أسباب خاصة، وهذا يفيد علماً عادياً بالإجماع على عدم منع خصوص السبب عموم اللفظ وذلك (كآية (السرقة) تمسكوا بها وهي واردة في سرقة المجن أو رداء صفوان بن أمية على ما ذكر في بعض التفاسير وآية الظهار ) نزلت في سلمة البياضي) هكذا في كتب الأصول والذي في كتب الحديث أن سلمة ظاهر امرأته، فأمره صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالكفارة، وأعطى من مال الصدقات ما يكفر به أو أوس بن السامت) هكذا وجدت نسخ المتن، وفي كتب الحديث بالصاد والقصة أن الظهار كان طلاقاً في الجاهلية، فجاءت خولة امرأة أوس بن الصامت إلى رسول الله فأخبرته الخبر، وقد كان قال أوس ما أرى إلا وقد حرمت كما في رواية ،الطبراني، فانطلقت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وجادلت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأنزل الله تعالى: ﴿قَدْ سَمِعَ اللهُ قَوْلَ الَّتِي تُجَدِلُكَ فِي زَوْجِهَا ﴾ [المجادلة: ١] وهذا ثابت في الصحاح والسنن وآية اللعان) نزلت في هلال بن أمية) كما في «صحيح البخاري وغيره وقصته أنه وجد شريكاً على امرأته فذكر لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : «البينة أو حد في ظهرك فقال : يا رسول الله ، إذا رأى أحدنا على امرأته رجلاً ينطلق يلتمس البينة، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، مقالته فقال والذي بعثك بالحق، إني لصادق والله يبرىء ظهري عن الحد، فنزلت آية اللعان (أو) (عويمر) كما في الصحيحين إلى غير ذلك) يطول الكلام بذكره، المخصصون بالسبب (قالوا : أولاً لو كان الوارد في سبب خاص (عاماً لجاز تخصيص السبب) عنه (بالاجتهاد) لأن نسبته إليه كنسبة سائر الأفراد التي يجوز تخصيصها بالاجتهاد إما مطلقاً أو بن صخر بمنع بطلان بعد تخصيصه بقطعي، والتالي باطل بالإجماع (قلنا : الملازمة ممنوعة للقطع بدخوله، فإنه جواب والمطابقة واجبة فهذه المطابقة قرينة الدخول والتخصيص بالاجتهاد إنما يجوز للإفراد التي لم تدل القرينة على دخولها قطعاً فليس نسبته كنسبة سائر الأفراد
The third article on linguistic principles. [Example of] the well of Buda'a when a questioner asked about its water into which menstrual cloths are thrown: 'The water is pure, nothing makes it impure' narrated by Ahmad, Tirmidhi, and Abu Dawud. This example is only valid if the lam is not for the covenant as some Hanafis said that the water of the well of Buda'a was flowing in gardens, and this is a reference to it in response to the argument of Malik's followers with this hadith for the purity of all water. The details are mentioned in Fath al-Qadir, Fath al-Mannan, and Sharh Safar al-Sa'ada. Or a specific cause other than a question as narrated that he passed by a sheep of Maymuna and said: 'Any hide that is tanned is purified' - the hadith is authentic as in Fath al-Qadir and others, but it is not reported that it occurred regarding a sheep of Maymuna; what occurred regarding her is his saying: 'Why did you not benefit from its hide?' They said: 'It is carrion.' He said: 'Its eating is only forbidden.' Narrated by the two Shaykhs. According to the majority of Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis: consideration is for the generality of the wording, acting upon it, not for the specific cause, so that the ruling is specified. And what is reported from al-Shafi'i is the opposite: consideration is for the specific cause, not for the generality of the wording. It is said this is a mistake. The author indicated its refutation by saying: 'And Imam al-Haramayn authenticated it, for he is more knowledgeable of his madhhab.' In some commentaries of al-Minhaj, it is an error of the Imam. Al-Shafi'i stated in his book called al-Umm that consideration is for the generality of the wording. Imam al-Razi strongly rebuked those who attribute this saying to al-Shafi'i and attributed this saying to Imam Malik, Abu Thawr, and al-Muzani. For us, firstly: the wording is general, it is placed for generality, so it must be acted upon unless there is a preventing factor. No preventing factor is imagined except its occurrence on a specific cause. A specific cause is not suitable as a preventer diverting it from what it is placed for, and it does not prevent acting upon it as required, and this is apparent. And for us, secondly: the adherence of the Companions and those after them, without disapproval, to generalities that occurred on specific causes. This yields customary knowledge of consensus that a specific cause does not prevent the generality of the wording. Such as the verse of theft; they adhered to it while it occurred regarding a shield or the cloak of Safwan ibn Umayya as mentioned in some exegeses. And the verse of zihar; it was revealed regarding Salama al-Bayadi (or Aws ibn al-Samit) - thus I found copies of the text. In hadith books, it is that Salama pronounced zihar on his wife, so the Prophet ordered him to expiate and gave him from charity money to expiate, or Aws ibn al-Samit. In hadith books, the story is that zihar was divorce in the Jahiliyya. Khawla, the wife of Aws ibn al-Samit, came to the Messenger of Allah and informed him; Aws had said 'I think she has become forbidden' as in Tabarani's narration. She went to the Messenger of Allah and argued with him, so Allah revealed 'Allah has heard the saying of her who argues with you concerning her husband' [Mujadila:1]. This is established in Sahihs and Sunans. And the verse of li'an was revealed regarding Hilal ibn Umayya as in Sahih al-Bukhari and others; his story is that he found a partner with his wife, so he mentioned to the Messenger of Allah who said: 'Evidence or a hadd on your back.' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if one of us sees a man with his wife, he goes to seek evidence?' The Messenger of Allah repeated his saying. He said: 'By Him who sent you with truth, I am truthful, and Allah will clear my back from the hadd.' So the verse of li'an was revealed. Or regarding 'Uwaymir as in the two Sahihs, and so on; the discourse would be long to mention them. The objectors regarding the cause said: Firstly, if that which occurred on a specific cause is general, then it would be permissible to specify the cause from it by ijtihad, because its relation to it is like the relation of other individuals that are permissible to specify by ijtihad, either absolutely or... by preventing invalidity after specifying it with a definitive proof, and the consequent is false by consensus. We said: The entailment is denied due to the certainty of its inclusion, for it is an answer and correspondence is obligatory, so this correspondence is a contextual indication of inclusion, and specification by ijtihad is only permissible for individuals for which the contextual indication does not prove their inclusion definitively, so its relation is not like the relation of other individuals.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage begins the third article on linguistic principles in the book. It first presents a hadith example about the well of Buda'a, clarifying that the generality of the wording (الماء طهور) is what matters, not that the hadith was about a specific well. The text then states the dominant position of the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools: consideration is for the generality of the wording, not the specific occasion of revelation. A contrary opinion attributed to al-Shafi'i is dismissed as erroneous; the author notes that Imam al-Haramayn authenticated the correct view, and al-Shafi'i himself affirmed the general rule in his book al-Umm. The text then provides two proofs for the Hanafi position. First, the wording is general by linguistic function, so it must be applied unless there is a preventer; the specific occasion is not a valid preventer. Second, the Companions consistently applied general verses that were revealed on specific occasions, such as the theft verse (revealed about a specific case) and the zihar and li'an verses; this establishes a practical consensus that the specific cause does not restrict the general wording. The passage then presents the counterargument: if the wording is general, one could exclude the specific occasion by ijtihad, just like any other individual. The Hanafi response is that the specific occasion is definitively included because the wording is an answer to a question, and the correspondence between question and answer requires inclusion. Thus, the specific occasion cannot be excluded by ijtihad. The passage follows the author's order: position, proof, objection, response.

Key Terms
العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب (al-'ibra li'umum al-lafz la li'khusus al-sabab): The ruling is based on the generality of the wording, not the specific occasion that prompted it.
اللام للعهد (al-lam li'l-'ahd): The definite article 'al-' referring to a specific known entity (the well of Buda'a), rather than for generality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the author gives for the rule that generality of wording is not restricted by the specific occasion?
A) The literal meaning of the word 'عام'
B) The practice of the Companions applying general verses to all cases
C) The hadith about the well of Buda'a
D) Consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that general wording revealed on a specific occasion applies universally, and the specific cause cannot be excluded by ijtihad because the wording is an answer demanding correspondence.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Defense of Takhsis: The Slave-Girl Child and 'Al-Walad lil-Firash'
Defends Abu Hanifa's takhsis of the hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' by interpreting 'firash' as requiring acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school restricts the general hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' to cases where the master acknowledges the child, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on tahqiq al-manat.

Core Idea
The Hanafi interpretation of 'firash' requires acknowledgment, so the child of a slave-girl without iqrar is excluded from the hadith's generality.

This passage defends Abu Hanifa's ruling that the child of a cohabited slave-girl is not attributed to the master unless the master acknowledges the child. Critics claim this contradicts the general hadith 'al-walad lil-firash'. The author systematically refutes this, explaining the Hanafi usul principle that the term 'firash' in the hadith is understood in a specific legal sense requiring acknowledgment (iqrar). The discussion involves the famous incident of Zam'a's slave-girl, and the author shows that the Prophet's ruling there actually supports the Hanafi position when properly interpreted.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed case
Identify the legal issue: the child of a slave-girl cohabited by her master. Hanafi: not attributed without acknowledgment; Shafi'i: attributed automatically.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical difference.
2
Identify the proof
The Shafi'i proof is the general hadith 'al-walad lil-firash'. The Hanafi argument focuses on defining 'firash'.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, allowing for ijtihad in its application.
3
Analyze the Hanafi definition of firash
According to the text, 'firash' is a metaphor for lawful intercourse with the condition of the master's claim (da'wa) or acknowledgment. This is supported by the narration of Imam Abu Yusuf where acknowledgment was used as evidence.
The master's acknowledgment is not merely a condition but a constitutive element of the legal meaning of 'firash'.
4
Address the Shafi'i tahqiq al-manat objection
The Shafi'i argue that the cause (illah) is istifrash (taking as a concubine), not acknowledgment. The Hanafi response: tahqiq al-manat is not definitive; ijtihad can differentiate. The specific case of Zam'a is distinguished because her child was acknowledged (she was an umm walad).
The word 'walida' (slave-girl) in the report indicates she had already given birth, implying prior acknowledgment.
5
Conclude the practical consequence
Without acknowledgment, the child is a slave in Hanafi fiqh; in Shafi'i fiqh, the child is free and attributed to the master even without acknowledgment.
This difference stems from the usul disagreement over the definition of 'firash'.

فلو سلم فليس ضاراً، لأن هذا معنى شرعي عرف بالقرائن، وأما كونها موطوءة أو منكوحة كما عليه الشافعي فليس مفهوماً في العرف ولا مشار إليه في الشرع بخلاف الإقرار، فإنه مشار إليه في رواية أبي يوسف رحمه الله،
